# Commit 5a9e548ae8

**Date:** 2026-03-06T00:21  
**Author:** Michael Schürig <michael@schuerig.de>

## Commit message

Update docs and fix logging from code review findings

- Glossary: remove stale entries (Note1/Note2, Narrowing/Widening Factor,
  Regional Range, Range Mean, Adaptive Note Strategy), add missing entries
  (Training Mode, TrainingModeConfig, ProgressTimeline, EWMA, TimeBucket,
  DirectedInterval, TrainingConstants), clarify cent terminology, update
  Initial Cent Offset range (±100 → ±20)
- Architecture: add code review amendment documenting domain type threading,
  constant extraction, training modes, and logging standards
- Project context: add PitchMatchingSession state machine, ProgressTimeline
  as view dependency, domain type usage rules, Duration for time intervals,
  logging rules, interval training constraints
- check-dependencies.sh: fix feature directory name (Comparison → PitchComparison),
  add print() detection rule
- TrainingDataStore: replace print() with os.Logger at .warning level
- arc42 glossary: sync with main glossary updates

Co-Authored-By: Claude Opus 4.6 <noreply@anthropic.com>

<command-message>bmad-bmm-code-review</command-message>
<command-name>/bmad-bmm-code-review</command-name>
<command-args>I want you to do a whole-project code review. Things I want you to look for

* raw types and literals where domain types exist
  * note values
  * timeInterval instead of duration
  * assumptions about the MIDI note range
* constants in algorithm and session implementations that should be extracted to configuration classes
* spurious dependencies between components
  * look for opportunities to apply dependency inversion. use good taste.
* duplicate terminology and terminology creep.
* code duplication
* sensible logging and tastefully used log-level.
* glossary
  * missing concepts
    * e.g., training modes are missing, although I'm unclear whether we really want to use that term or if there's something better
  * outdated concepts
    * e.g., the glossary still contains note1, note2, narrowing/widening factors, weak spots, and lots more

Apart from finding concrete places in the code that need refactoring, I also want you to make suggestions for improvements to
* architecture.md
* glossary.md
* project-context.md
* bin/check-dependencies.sh
* other documents

This is a tall order and I expect you to carry it out thoroughly and diligently. If you find cases where you are unsure, do not hesitate to ask me.</command-args>

- **Total Issues Found**: ~50+ locations across production code
- **Severity**: Medium to High (affects type safety, semantic clarity, and maintainability)
- **Category Distribution**:
  - Raw Int for MIDI notes: ~15 locations
  - Raw Double for Cents: ~12 locations  
  - Raw TimeInterval for NoteDuration: ~4 locations
  - Raw Double for Frequency: ~4 locations
  - Raw Double for UnitInterval: ~5 locations
  - Raw Int for Interval: ~8 locations
  - Hard-coded magic numbers (0, 127): ~8 locations

### Key Architectural Constraints

1. **SwiftData Models** (PitchComparisonRecord, PitchMatchingRecord): Limited to primitive types for persistence. Would require a persistence mapping layer to fully adopt domain types.

2. **AppStorage** (SettingsScreen, SettingsKeys): AppStorage requires primitive types. Workaround would be custom property wrappers or intermediate conversion layer.

3. **CSV Import/Export**: Currently uses primitives for data transfer. Should standardize on domain types in business logic and only convert at I/O boundaries.</result>

- `/Users/michael/Projekte/peach/Peach/PitchComparison/PitchComparisonFeedbackIndicator.swift`
- `/Users/michael/Projekte/peach/Peach/PitchMatching/PitchMatchingFeedbackIndicator.swift`

**Analysis:**
These are intentionally different - PitchComparison shows correct/incorrect thumbs icons (lines 34-36), while PitchMatching shows directional arrows with numerical feedback (lines 22-32). However, there's potential for sharing:

**Shared Logic:**
- Accessibility label generation logic (both have hand-rolled accessibility)
- Icon sizing calculations could be consolidated
- FeedbackBand color mapping (PitchMatching lines 73-79) shares color semantics with implicit correctness colors in PitchComparison

**Recommended Improvement:**
Create a shared `FeedbackColorScheme` utility enum for consistent color semantics across feedback types.

---

### 4. OBSERVER PROTOCOLS - Semantic Duplication

**Files:**
- `/Users/michael/Projekte/peach/Peach/Core/Training/PitchComparisonObserver.swift` (30 lines)
- `/Users/michael/Projekte/peach/Peach/Core/Training/PitchMatchingObserver.swift` (18 lines)

**Issue:**
These protocols serve identical purposes but are type-specific. Both:
- Have identical docstring structure
- List identical conforming types (TrainingDataStore, PerceptualProfile)
- Follow identical observer pattern

**Recommended Refactoring:**
Consider a generic `TrainingObserver<Result>` protocol or a unified observer with associated type, eliminating the need for two nearly-identical protocol definitions.

---

### 5. PROFILE PROTOCOLS - Terminology Inconsistency

**Files:**
- `/Users/michael/Projekte/peach/Peach/Core/Profile/PitchComparisonProfile.swift`
- `/Users/michael/Projekte/peach/Peach/Core/Profile/PitchMatchingProfile.swift`
- `/Users/michael/Projekte/peach/Peach/Core/Profile/PerceptualProfile.swift` (unified implementation)

**Terminology Issues - Same Concept, Different Names:**

| Concept | PitchComparison | PitchMatching |
|---------|-----------------|---------------|
| Update method | `update(note:centOffset:isCorrect:)` | `updateMatching(note:centError:)` |
| Mean property | `overallMean` | `matchingMean` |
| Std Dev property | `overallStdDev` | `matchingStdDev` |
| Sample count | implicit in stats | `matchingSampleCount` |
| Reset method | `reset()` | `resetMatching()` |

**Root Cause:**
Different semantic models: PitchComparison tracks "offset" (magnitude of difficulty), while PitchMatching tracks "error" (user accuracy). However, both measure deviation and could use unified terminology.

**Recommended Solution:**
Unify to either "deviation" or "error" terminology across both profiles. The data model uses different structures (centOffset vs. centError in records), but the profile interface could normalize to a common term like `updateAccuracy(note:deviation:)` or `updatePerformance(note:centDeviation:isCorrect:)`.

---

### 6. DOMAIN TYPE DUPLICATION - Data Records

**Files:**
- `/Users/michael/Projekte/peach/Peach/Core/Data/PitchComparisonRecord.swift`
- `/Users/michael/Projekte/peach/Peach/Core/Data/PitchMatchingRecord.swift`

**Shared Fields:**
- `referenceNote: Int`
- `targetNote: Int`
- `interval: Int`
- `tuningSystem: String`
- `timestamp: Date`

**Differences:**
- PitchComparison has: `centOffset`, `isCorrect`
- PitchMatching has: `initialCentOffset`, `userCentError`

**Recommended Refactoring:**
Create a base `TrainingRecord` protocol or class with common fields, allowing both to specialize. This reduces duplication in initialization and storage logic.

---

### 7. SESSION STATE ENUMS - Semantic Duplication

**Files:**
- `PitchComparisonSessionState` (5 cases, line 5-11)
- `PitchMatchingSessionState` (5 cases, line 5-11)

**Comparison:**

| State | Comparison | Matching | Semantic Equivalence |
|-------|-----------|----------|----------------------|
| idle | ✓ | ✓ | Same |
| playingNote1 | ✓ | - | Different workflows |
| playingNote2 | ✓ | - | Part of playingReference |
| playingReference | - | ✓ | Equivalent to playingNote1 |
| awaitingAnswer | ✓ | - | Same semantically |
| awaitingSliderTouch | - | ✓ | Different UX patterns |
| playingTunable | - | ✓ | Active adjustment state |
| showingFeedback | ✓ | ✓ | Same |

**Opportunity:**
States are necessarily different due to fundamentally different workflows (comparison vs. slider matching). No unification recommended here—this is correct domain design.

### 8. CONFIGURATION PATTERNS - Repeated Constants

**Files:**
- `PitchComparisonSession.swift` lines 40-59
- `PitchMatchingSession.swift` lines 54-57, 200-211

**Duplicated Configuration:**
- `velocity: MIDIVelocity = 63` (both files)
- `feedbackDuration: TimeInterval = 0.4` (both files)
- Settings derivation logic (TrainingSettings wrapping)

**Recommended Consolidation:**
Create a `TrainingSessionConstants` enum or config struct to centralize these shared configuration values.

---

### 9. TERMINOLOGY CONFLICTS - Cent Measurements

**Found in 15+ files:**

| Term | Used In | Meaning |
|------|---------|---------|
| `centOffset` | PitchComparisonRecord, PerceptualProfile, PitchMatchingSession | Deviation/displacement |
| `centError` | PitchMatchingRecord, PitchMatchingObserver, PitchMatchingFeedbackIndicator | User's inaccuracy |
| `offset` (magnitude) | PitchComparison, PerceptualProfile | Difficulty measure |

**Semantic Confusion:**
- In pitch comparison: "offset" = the difficulty (how far apart notes are)
- In pitch matching: "error" = user's accuracy (how far from target)
- Both represent signed deviations in cents, but terminology differs

**Affected Files:**
- `/Users/michael/Projekte/peach/Peach/Core/Profile/PerceptualProfile.swift` (lines 33-36, 119-125) - uses both terms
- `/Users/michael/Projekte/peach/Peach/PitchMatching/PitchMatchingFeedbackIndicator.swift` (lines 51-89) - uses centError
- `/Users/michael/Projekte/peach/Peach/Core/Data/CSVImportParser.swift` - imports with centOffset column name

**Recommended Unification:**
Adopt "centDeviation" as the umbrella term, with domain-specific qualifiers:
- "difficulty" for comparison's offset
- "userError" or "userDeviation" for matching's accuracy deviation

---

1. **HIGH**: Extract shared session state management into a base class or extended protocol (affects both session classes)
2. **HIGH**: Consolidate terminology around cent measurements (standardize on "deviation" vs. "error")
3. **MEDIUM**: Extract common screen lifecycle patterns (help sheet, toolbar, lifecycle handlers)
4. **MEDIUM**: Create generic or base observer protocol to eliminate duplicate observer definitions
5. **MEDIUM**: Consolidate record types with a common base (TrainingRecord)
6. **MEDIUM**: Centralize shared configuration constants (velocity, feedbackDuration)
7. **LOW**: Create FeedbackColorScheme utility for consistent color semantics

These refactorings would reduce code duplication by approximately 15-20% while improving maintainability and semantic consistency across the domain.</result>

## COMPREHENSIVE LOGGING ANALYSIS REPORT

### Executive Summary

The Peach codebase demonstrates **good logging infrastructure** with a consistent approach using Apple's `os.Logger` framework. Logging is well-established across critical components, but there are areas where logging can be enhanced:

1. **Strengths:** Centralized Logger setup, appropriate log levels in most cases, good coverage of state machines and audio lifecycle
2. **Weaknesses:** Use of `print()` statements instead of proper logging, missing lifecycle logging in some audio paths, inconsistent format between imports (`import os` vs `import OSLog`)
3. **Gaps:** Missing logging in error recovery paths, some observer completion patterns lack details

---

### 2. LOGGING CONSISTENCY ANALYSIS

#### **Log Levels Used:**
- ✅ `info` - Lifecycle, state transitions, user actions, challenge/comparison setup (most common, appropriate)
- ✅ `warning` - Invalid state transitions, parse failures, unknown enum cases, audio issues
- ✅ `debug` - Non-critical state changes, detailed metrics, scene phase changes
- ✅ `error` - Audio errors, unexpected exceptions (appropriate)
- ❌ `fault` - Not used (would be appropriate for catastrophic failures)

#### **Subsystem/Category Pattern:**
All loggers follow consistent naming:
```swift
Logger(subsystem: "com.peach.app", category: "{ComponentName}")
```
✅ Excellent consistency across all components

#### **Import Inconsistency:**
- 7 files use: `import os` (recommended)
- 2 files use: `import OSLog` (older style, equivalent)
- **Issue:** Inconsistent - should standardize on `import os`

### 3. CRITICAL ISSUES FOUND

#### **Issue 1: `print()` in TrainingDataStore (HIGH PRIORITY)**
**File:** `/Users/michael/Projekte/peach/Peach/Core/Data/TrainingDataStore.swift`
**Lines:** 125, 127, 154, 157
**Problem:** Observer error handling uses `print()` instead of Logger
**Impact:**
- Errors cannot be filtered by log level
- Not captured by OS Log tools
- Cannot be controlled via OS_LOG_TYPE environment variable
- Lost in console noise
**Recommendation:** Replace all `print()` with proper logger calls

#### **Issue 2: Missing Audio Lifecycle Logging (MEDIUM PRIORITY)**
**File:** `/Users/michael/Projekte/peach/Peach/Core/Audio/SoundFontNotePlayer.swift`
**Problem:** No logging for:
- `play()` entry/exit
- `stopAll()` entry/exit
- Preset load failures (silently falls back to default)
- Audio session configuration
- Frequency validation errors
**Impact:** Difficult to diagnose audio issues or preset switching failures
**Recommendation:** Add info-level logging for:
- Successful note play attempts
- Stop operations
- Preset load failures with error details

**Impact:** User answering during a race condition (UI responding before state update) triggers error log, but this is recoverable

#### **Issue 5: Inconsistent Logger Creation Pattern (LOW PRIORITY)**

// Line 21-22: Creates new logger inline (should use instance)

    .warning("Failed to parse SF2 at \(url.lastPathComponent): \(error)")
```
**Recommendation:** Use `logger.warning()` consistently

#### **Issue 6: Async Logging Order Issue (LOW PRIORITY)**

**Line:** 175
**Problem:** Logs after spawning a Task without await
```swift

    try? await notePlayer.stopAll()

}
```
**Impact:** Log message may appear after subsequent events
**Recommendation:** Log before spawning async task, or log in the completion

### 5. STRENGTHS IN LOGGING PRACTICES

1. **Session State Machines:** Both `PitchComparisonSession` and `PitchMatchingSession` have excellent logging of:
   - State transitions with current state
   - User actions with details (e.g., "HIGHER" vs "LOWER")
   - Challenge/comparison setup with all parameters
   - Detailed result metrics

2. **Numeric Precision:** Logging includes:
   - Frequency values in Hz
   - Cent offsets with decimal precision
   - Statistical measures (mean, stdDev, sample count)
   - Performance metrics (profile load time in ms)

3. **Audio System:** Good coverage of:
   - Interruption events (began/ended)
   - Route changes with reasons
   - Device state transitions
   - Preset switches

4. **Lifecycle Tracking:** Good logging of:
   - Component initialization
   - Screen appear/disappear
   - App backgrounding/foregrounding
   - Training loop entry/exit

5. **Graceful Error Handling:** Errors are logged with:
   - Error descriptions via `error.localizedDescription`
   - Context of what was being attempted
   - Decision made (e.g., "stopping training")

| **LOW** | Error level too severe for race condition | Change to warning | PitchComparisonSession: 133 |
| **OPTIONAL** | Import inconsistency | Standardize on `import os` | KazezNoteStrategy, PerceptualProfile (change from OSLog) |

---

### 7. OBSERVED PATTERNS & CONVENTIONS

All Logger instances follow this pattern:
```swift
private let logger = Logger(subsystem: "com.peach.app", category: "{ComponentName}")
```

Exception: `AudioSessionInterruptionMonitor` receives Logger via dependency injection (appropriate for testability)

Log messages are structured as:
- **Action/Event:** "Challenge:", "Result:", "Answer was", "stopped", "initialized"
- **Detailed Parameters:** values, frequencies, notes, durations
- **State Context:** current state, previous state, transition reason

Format is **human-readable and debugger-friendly** with good use of string interpolation.

---

### 8. SENSITIVE DATA CHECK

No sensitive data observed in logging:
- No passwords, tokens, or authentication credentials
- No personal user data beyond training metrics
- No file paths that could leak system information
- Audio parameters and note values are appropriate for logging

✅ **No security concerns identified**

---

## CONCLUSION

The Peach codebase has **good logging infrastructure** with:
- ✅ Consistent Logger setup and naming conventions
- ✅ Appropriate log levels in most cases
- ✅ Excellent state machine transition logging
- ✅ Good audio lifecycle coverage
- ✅ Detailed metric logging with numeric precision

However, improvements needed:
- ❌ Replace `print()` with proper Logger in TrainingDataStore
- ❌ Add audio lifecycle logging to SoundFontNotePlayer
- ❌ Fix log level severity issues (device disconnect, race condition)
- ❌ Standardize import style
- ⚠️ Consider adding observer callback logging for debugging

## Code Review: Dependencies and Coupling Analysis

I've completed a thorough analysis of the Peach iOS project's dependencies and coupling. Here are my findings:

### 1. STRENGTHS (Architectural Successes)

**Clean Layering**
- `/Users/michael/Projekte/peach/Peach/Core/` is perfectly framework-free (no SwiftUI, UIKit, Charts imports)
- SwiftData correctly confined to `Core/Data/` and `App/` only
- Feature directories (`PitchComparison/`, `PitchMatching/`, `Profile/`, `Settings/`, `Info/`) have no cross-feature type references
- Charts properly isolated to Profile view layer

**Protocol-First Design**
- `/Users/michael/Projekte/peach/Peach/Core/Audio/NotePlayer.swift`: Protocol abstraction with implementations injected (line 12)
- `/Users/michael/Projekte/peach/Peach/Core/Audio/SoundSourceProvider.swift`: Excellent protocol design (line 1-4)
- `/Users/michael/Projekte/peach/Peach/Settings/UserSettings.swift`: Core abstraction (lines 3-11)
- Profile uses protocol boundaries: `PitchComparisonProfile`, `PitchMatchingProfile` (not concrete PerceptualProfile) injected into sessions
- Sessions depend on protocols: `NotePlayer`, `NextPitchComparisonStrategy`, `PitchComparisonProfile` (lines 29-31 of PitchComparisonSession.swift)

**Observer Pattern Properly Implemented**
- `/Users/michael/Projekte/peach/Peach/Core/Training/PitchComparisonObserver.swift`: Clean decoupling with observer array
- Multiple conformers (TrainingDataStore, PerceptualProfile, HapticFeedbackManager, ProgressTimeline) at `PeachApp.swift:158`

**Composition Root Well-Designed**
- `/Users/michael/Projekte/peach/Peach/App/PeachApp.swift`: All services instantiated centrally (lines 20-82)
- All environment keys properly injected via `@Environment` (lines 90-101)
- Dependency closure pattern for complex coordination (dataStoreResetter at line 96)

**Views Are Thin**
- Screens only interact with injected session objects
- No direct access to NotePlayer, TrainingDataStore, or concrete implementations
- PitchComparisonScreen and PitchMatchingScreen use only @Environment for dependencies
- No Combine imports anywhere (correctly using async/await)

---

### 2. ISSUES FOUND

**Issue #1: Redundant Profile Reset Logic**
- **Location**: `/Users/michael/Projekte/peach/Peach/App/PeachApp.swift`, lines 52-53
- **Problem**: In the `TrainingDataTransferService` callback (`onDataChanged`), code calls both `profile.reset()` and `profile.resetMatching()`. The `reset()` method clears both comparison and matching stats, making the second call redundant.
- **Evidence**: 
  - `PerceptualProfile.reset()` at line 105 resets `noteStats` array (clears everything)
  - `PerceptualProfile.resetMatching()` at line 141 only resets matching counters
  - After `profile.reset()` at line 52, the `resetMatching()` call at line 53 is unnecessary
- **Impact**: Minor code smell, not a functional bug, but indicates unclear intent
- **Fix**: Remove line 53 or clarify the intent (perhaps only `resetMatching()` should be called since comparison stats get repopulated from imported records at lines 54-56)

**Issue #2: UIKit Coupling in Wrong File**
- **Location**: `/Users/michael/Projekte/peach/Peach/PitchComparison/HapticFeedbackManager.swift`, line 1
- **Status**: ACTUALLY CORRECT - This IS the approved exception. Project context specifies UIKit only allowed in `Comparison/HapticFeedbackManager.swift` and `App/`
- **Check-dependencies.sh Validation**: Script at line 91 correctly allows this via exclusion pattern

**Issue #3: SettingsScreen Has Minimal Coupling Surface**
- **Location**: `/Users/michael/Projekte/peach/Peach/Settings/SettingsScreen.swift`, lines 29-31
- **Dependencies Injected**: 3 (@Environment dependencies)
  - `dataStoreResetter` (closure)
  - `soundSourceProvider` (protocol)
  - `trainingDataTransferService` (concrete class)
- **Justification**: This is appropriate - SettingsScreen correctly accesses services only via environment, not via direct service instantiation
- **All three are necessary**: No unused dependencies detected

---

### 3. DEPENDENCY INVERSION OPPORTUNITIES

- **Current**: Default initialized with `SoundFontLibrary()` (concrete type)
- **Note**: This is a preview stub, so acceptable. Production wiring at `PeachApp.swift:95` correctly injects the real instance
- **Status**: No change needed

**Minor Opportunity #2: TrainingDataTransferService is Not Protocol-Backed**

### 🤖 Assistant (2026-03-05T22:16)

I've completed the review and saved it to `docs/code-review-2026-03-05.md`.

Here's a summary of what I found:

**12 HIGH, 15 MEDIUM, 10 LOW** issues across 7 categories.

The biggest themes:

1. **Domain type erosion** -- `Cents`, `Frequency`, `MIDINote`, and `NoteDuration` types exist but are bypassed at persistence boundaries, profile interfaces, and the `NotePlayer` protocol. The most impactful fix is threading `NoteDuration` through `NotePlayer.play()` and `Cents` through `PerceptualProfile.update()`.

2. **Glossary is substantially outdated** -- Note1/Note2, narrowing/widening factors, regional ranges, Natural/Mechanical mode, and the "Adaptive Note Strategy" description all refer to a previous algorithm design. The actual Kazez formula uses completely different parameters. Training modes (the four unison/interval x comparison/matching categories) are a core concept missing entirely.

3. **Logging gaps** -- `TrainingDataStore` uses `print()` instead of `Logger` on error paths, and `SoundFontNotePlayer` has no lifecycle logging at all.

4. **Shared constants** -- `feedbackDuration` (0.4s) and `velocity` (63) are duplicated between the two session classes. The Kazez formula coefficients (0.05, 0.09) are undocumented magic numbers.

5. **Architecture is clean** -- No dependency violations found. The protocol boundaries, composition root, and observer patterns are well-designed. The `check-dependencies.sh` script has minor gaps but catches the important rules.

Want me to dive deeper into any of these findings, or shall we discuss which issues to tackle first?

<a id="msg-assistant-91"></a>

### 🤖 Assistant (2026-03-05T22:23)

Now I have a complete picture. Let me compile the deep-dive analysis.

Here's my systematic inventory of every raw constant and every extraction opportunity, organized by component.

---

## Deep Dive: Raw Constants and Configuration Extraction

### A. Algorithm Layer

#### `KazezNoteStrategy.swift` -- The heart of the adaptive algorithm

**Line 64**: `0.05` -- Kazez narrowing coefficient
**Line 68**: `0.09` -- Kazez widening coefficient

These two numbers control the entire difficulty curve. They're embedded inline in private methods with no name, no documentation, and no connection to the glossary (which still describes a completely different formula: "0.95 multiplier" and "1.3 multiplier"). The formula is `p * (1.0 - k * sqrt(p))` where `k` is either 0.05 or 0.09.

**Line 45**: `127` -- hardcoded MIDI upper bound
**Line 47**: `interval.interval.semitones` -- used as raw Int offset subtracted from 127

The note range clamping logic (`min(settings.noteRange.upperBound.rawValue, 127 - interval.interval.semitones)`) is duplicated exactly in `PitchMatchingSession.swift:220`. Both extract `.rawValue` from domain types to do raw Int arithmetic.

**Extraction opportunity**: The Kazez coefficients, the difficulty clamping range (`minCentDifference`...`maxCentDifference`), and the note range clamping logic are all algorithm parameters. Currently the coefficients are baked in while the difficulty bounds come from `TrainingSettings`. This is inconsistent -- either the Kazez factors should be injectable, or they should at least be named constants with documentation.

Suggested shape:
```swift
// On KazezNoteStrategy or a KazezConfig struct
static let narrowingCoefficient: Double = 0.05
static let wideningCoefficient: Double = 0.09
```

This is also an opportunity to document the formula derivation (presumably from Daniel Kazez's "The Interval" or similar).

---

#### `TrainingSettings` (in `NextPitchComparisonStrategy.swift`)

**Line 63**: `MIDINote(36)` -- default lower bound (C2)
**Line 63**: `MIDINote(84)` -- default upper bound (C6)
**Line 65**: `0.1` -- default minCentDifference
**Line 66**: `100.0` -- default maxCentDifference

These defaults are duplicated with `SettingsKeys.defaultNoteRangeMin/Max` (lines 17-18, using raw `Int` 36 and 84). The 0.1 and 100.0 cent bounds don't appear in `SettingsKeys` at all -- they're only in `TrainingSettings`.

**Problem**: Two sources of truth for note range defaults. `SettingsKeys` uses raw `Int`, `TrainingSettings` uses `MIDINote`. If someone changes one without the other, they silently diverge.

---

### B. Session Layer

#### `PitchComparisonSession.swift`

| Line | Constant | Type | Meaning |
|------|----------|------|---------|
| 55 | `5.0` | `Float` | Max loudness variation in dB |
| 57 | `63` | `MIDIVelocity` | MIDI velocity for all notes |
| 59 | `0.4` | `TimeInterval` | Feedback display duration (seconds) |
| 203 | `100` | `Int` (milliseconds) | Polling interval in training loop |

**Line 55, `maxLoudnessOffsetDB`**: A `Float` literal for a perceptual design constant. Controls how much the target note's volume varies to prevent the user from using loudness cues. Named, but not extracted to a shared location.

**Line 57, `velocity: MIDIVelocity = 63`**: MIDI velocity 63 is roughly mezzo-piano. This same value appears in `PitchMatchingSession.swift:56`. It's a musical/perceptual choice, not an implementation detail.

**Line 59, `feedbackDuration = 0.4`**: The 0.4-second feedback display is called out in `project-context.md:226` as a deliberate perceptual design decision. It's duplicated in `PitchMatchingSession.swift:57`. It also appears in the glossary as "Displays for 0.4 seconds" (line 105) and "~400ms" (line 107).

**Line 203, `Task.sleep(for: .milliseconds(100))`**: This is a polling loop that keeps the training loop alive. The 100ms interval is an implementation detail, but it's also a responsiveness parameter -- shorter = more responsive state transitions, longer = less CPU. Worth naming.

**Line 242-246, `calculateTargetAmplitude`**: The amplitude calculation uses `maxLoudnessOffsetDB` (named) but the `Float(varyLoudness)` conversion and `Float.random(in: -range...range)` embed the assumption that loudness variation is symmetric and uniform. This is a design choice.

#### `PitchMatchingSession.swift`

| Line | Constant | Type | Meaning |
|------|----------|------|---------|
| 54 | `-20.0...20.0` | `ClosedRange<Double>` | Initial cent offset range for challenges |
| 56 | `63` | `MIDIVelocity` | MIDI velocity (duplicate) |
| 57 | `0.4` | `TimeInterval` | Feedback duration (duplicate) |
| 131 | `1200.0` | `Double` | Cents per octave (physics constant) |
| 145 | `1200.0` | `Double` | Cents per octave (duplicate) |
| 220 | `127` | `Int` | MIDI upper bound (duplicate with Kazez) |
| 262 | `0.0` | `Double` | Reference note amplitude (always 0 dB) |

**Line 54, `initialCentOffsetRange`**: This ±20-cent range determines the maximum starting offset for pitch matching challenges. It directly affects difficulty. Currently a private static constant with a raw `Double` range instead of `Cents`. The glossary says "Random within ±100 cents for v0.2" -- which contradicts the code's ±20 cents. Either the glossary is stale or the value changed.

**Lines 131, 145, `1200.0`**: Cents-per-octave is a musical physics constant. It appears in two places within this file and also in `TuningSystem.swift:47,52`. This is the kind of constant that should be `Cents.perOctave` or similar.

**Line 262, `AmplitudeDB(0.0)`**: The reference note always plays at 0 dB (no loudness variation). PitchMatchingSession doesn't have the `varyLoudness` feature that PitchComparisonSession has. This asymmetry is a design choice but isn't documented.

---

### C. Profile Layer

#### `PerceptualProfile.swift`

| Line | Constant | Type | Meaning |
|------|----------|------|---------|
| 21 | `128` | `Int` | MIDI note count (array size) |
| 106 | `128` | `Int` | MIDI note count (reset) |
| 158 | `100.0` | `Double` | Default difficulty for cold start |

**Line 158, `currentDifficulty: Double = 100.0`**: This is the cold-start difficulty -- what the algorithm uses when it has no data for a note. It equals `TrainingSettings.maxCentDifference` by coincidence, not by reference. If someone changes the default max to 80 cents, the cold-start difficulty would still be 100.

**Lines 21, 106**: `128` is `MIDINote.validRange.count`. The array is indexed by `note.rawValue`, coupling the array size to the MIDI specification. Using `MIDINote.validRange.count` would make this explicit.

#### `PerceptualNote` (in `PerceptualProfile.swift`)

**Line 158**: All default field values (`mean: 0.0`, `stdDev: 0.0`, `m2: 0.0`, `sampleCount: 0`, `currentDifficulty: 100.0`) represent a cold-start state. `mean`, `stdDev`, `m2`, `sampleCount` at zero are mathematically correct for "no data." But `currentDifficulty: 100.0` is a tunable parameter masquerading as a default.

#### `ProgressTimeline.swift`

| Line | Constant | Type | Meaning |
|------|----------|------|---------|
| 333 | `24 * 3600` | `Double` | 1 day in seconds (bucket threshold) |
| 342 | `7 * 86400` | `Double` | 1 week in seconds (bucket threshold) |
| 344 | `86400` | `Double` | 1 day in seconds (day end calculation) |
| 346 | `30 * 86400` | `Double` | 30 days in seconds (bucket threshold) |
| 413 | `86400` | `Double` | 1 day in seconds (sub-bucket) |

These define the adaptive bucketing policy: records less than 24h old are bucketed per session, 1-7 days old per day, 7-30 days per week, older per month. This is a data visualization design decision that should be named:

```swift
private static let recentThreshold: TimeInterval = 24 * 3600
private static let weekThreshold: TimeInterval = 7 * 86400
private static let monthThreshold: TimeInterval = 30 * 86400
```

Or even better, these could live on `TrainingModeConfig` or a `BucketingConfig` struct if you anticipate wanting different bucketing per mode.

**Line 218, `recordCount >= 2`**: Minimum sample count for standard deviation. This is a statistical requirement (Bessel's correction), not a tunable parameter. Fine as-is.

#### `TrainingModeConfig.swift`

| Line | Constant | Meaning | Shared? |
|------|----------|---------|---------|
| 29 | `Cents(8.0)` | Unison comparison optimal baseline | Unique |
| 30 | `.seconds(7 * 86400)` | EWMA half-life (7 days) | Same across all 4 modes |
| 31 | `.seconds(1800)` | Session gap (30 minutes) | Same across all 4 modes |
| 37 | `Cents(12.0)` | Interval comparison optimal baseline | Unique |
| 45 | `Cents(5.0)` | Unison matching optimal baseline | Unique |
| 53 | `Cents(8.0)` | Interval matching optimal baseline | Unique |

The `ewmaHalflife` and `sessionGap` values are identical across all four modes. This is either intentional (same smoothing everywhere) or accidental (copy-paste from the first mode). If intentional, extract shared defaults:

```swift
private static let defaultEWMAHalflife: Duration = .seconds(7 * 86400)
private static let defaultSessionGap: Duration = .seconds(1800)
```

The optimal baselines (5, 8, 8, 12 cents) are the expert-level targets shown as dashed lines on the progress chart. These represent what a trained musician could achieve and are genuinely mode-specific.

---

### D. Audio Layer

#### `SoundFontNotePlayer.swift`

| Line | Constant | Type | Meaning |
|------|----------|------|---------|
| 24 | `0` | `UInt8` | MIDI channel |
| 25 | `0x79` | `UInt8` | Default bank MSB (melodic) |
| 26 | `8192` | `UInt16` | Pitch bend center value |
| 27 | `20.0...20000.0` | `ClosedRange<Double>` | Valid frequency range (Hz) |
| 34 | `80` | `Int` | Default preset program (Sine Wave) |
| 35 | `8` | `Int` | Default preset bank |
| 47 | `.milliseconds(25)` | `Duration` | Stop propagation delay default |
| 79-82 | `0...127` | Range | MIDI program/bank validation range |
| 101 | `.milliseconds(20)` | `Duration` | Post-preset-load settling time |
| 180-183 | `101, 100, 6, 38, 2, 0` | MIDI CC | Pitch bend range RPN |
| 199 | `8192.0`, `200.0` | `Double` | Pitch bend calculation constants |
| 208-212 | `69, 12.0, 100.0, 440.0, 0...127` | Various | MIDI decompose constants |

The MIDI constants (lines 180-183) are standard RPN (Registered Parameter Numbers) for setting pitch bend range. The values `101, 100, 6, 38` are MIDI CC numbers with established meanings:
- CC 101 = RPN MSB
- CC 100 = RPN LSB  
- CC 6 = Data Entry MSB (value `2` = ±2 semitones = ±200 cents)
- CC 38 = Data Entry LSB

**Line 182, `withValue: 2`**: This `2` sets the pitch bend range to ±2 semitones. It's the most important tunable here -- changing it affects pitch bend precision across the entire app. It directly corresponds to the `200.0` in `pitchBendValue()` at line 199 and the `200.0` guard in `SoundFontPlaybackHandle.swift:55`. These three values are coupled but not connected by a shared constant.

**Lines 208-212**: The `decompose` function has well-named local constants (`referenceMIDINote`, `semitonesPerOctave`, `centsPerSemitone`, `concert440`, `midiRange`). Good practice -- these are the right choice for function-local scope since they're MIDI specification constants, not tunable parameters.

**Line 47, `stopPropagationDelay`**: Already properly injected as a constructor parameter with a sensible default. Tests pass `.zero` for instant playback. This is the gold standard for how the other constants should work.

**Lines 79-82, `(0...127).contains(program/bank)`**: These validate MIDI program and bank numbers. While they happen to match `MIDINote.validRange`, they're conceptually different -- MIDI programs 0-127 are not the same as MIDI notes 0-127. I wouldn't unify these.

#### `SoundFontPlaybackHandle.swift`

| Line | Constant | Type | Meaning |
|------|----------|------|---------|
| 51 | `100.0` | `Double` | Cents per semitone (in decompose conversion) |
| 53 | `100.0` | `Double` | Cents per semitone (in cent difference calc) |
| 55 | `200.0` | `Double` | Max pitch bend range in cents |

**Line 55, `200.0`**: This is the ±200-cent pitch bend guard. It must match the pitch bend range set by `sendPitchBendRange()`. Currently hardcoded as a magic number. If the pitch bend range in `SoundFontNotePlayer` changed from 2 to 4 semitones, this guard would be silently wrong.

#### `SoundFontLibrary.swift`

**Line 18**: `$0.bank < 120 && $0.program < 120` -- Filter for pitched presets. Bank >= 120 and program >= 120 indicate percussion/unpitched instruments in General MIDI. The thresholds 120 are spec-defined but undocumented in the code.

#### `HapticFeedbackManager.swift`

**Line 28**: `.heavy` -- Haptic intensity style
**Line 40**: `.milliseconds(50)` -- Delay between double-tap haptic impacts

The double-tap pattern with 50ms gap is a perceptual design choice for "noticeability." Named in the comment ("Brief second impact for more noticeable feedback") but not a named constant.

---

### E. View Layer (selected constants worth noting)

#### `VerticalPitchSlider.swift`

| Line | Constant | Meaning |
|------|----------|---------|
| 20 | `80` | Thumb width |
| 21 | `60` | Thumb height |
| 36 | `12` | Corner radius |
| 63 | `0.4` | Inactive opacity |
| 69 | `0.1` | Accessibility step size |

The `0.1` accessibility step at line 69 means VoiceOver users adjust in 10% increments. Since the slider maps to ±20 cents, each step is ±2 cents. This coupling between the accessibility step and the cent offset range is implicit.

#### `PitchMatchingFeedbackIndicator.swift`

| Line | Constant | Meaning |
|------|----------|---------|
| 13 | `100` | Default icon size |
| 14 | `40` | Close-match icon size |
| 15 | `70` | Moderate-match icon size |
| 40-48 | `0, 10, 30` | Band thresholds in cents |

**Lines 40-48**: The feedback bands (`deadCenter` at 0, `close` < 10, `moderate` <= 30, `far` > 30 cents) are the thresholds that determine what color and size arrow the user sees. These are perceptual design decisions. The glossary mentions different values: "Green dot for dead center (~0 cents), short green arrow (<10 cents), medium yellow arrow (10-30 cents), long red arrow (>30 cents)" -- which matches the code, but the thresholds are only defined in this view.

**Extraction opportunity**: If the matching algorithm ever needs to know about these bands (e.g., for scoring or gamification), they'd need to be duplicated. Consider a shared `FeedbackBand.threshold` pattern.

#### `PitchComparisonScreen.swift` and `PitchMatchingScreen.swift`

Both have `feedbackAnimation` returning `.easeInOut(duration: 0.2)`. This 0.2s animation duration is a UI polish constant, distinct from the 0.4s feedback display duration.

---

### F. Proposed Configuration Architecture

Looking at all the constants together, I see three natural groupings:

**1. Shared training constants** (used by both sessions):
- `feedbackDuration: TimeInterval = 0.4`
- `velocity: MIDIVelocity = 63`
- `centsPerOctave: Double = 1200.0`

**2. Algorithm constants** (Kazez-specific):
- `narrowingCoefficient: Double = 0.05`
- `wideningCoefficient: Double = 0.09`
- `coldStartDifficulty: Cents = 100.0`

**3. Pitch matching constants**:
- `initialCentOffsetRange: ClosedRange<Cents> = -20.0...20.0`

**4. Audio constants** (pitch bend configuration):
- `pitchBendRangeSemitones: Int = 2` (used to derive the RPN value, the 200-cent guard, and the pitch bend calculation divisor)

The question is: do you want `struct TrainingConstants` with static lets? Or do you want these injected as configuration at construction time (like `stopPropagationDelay` already is)? 

For constants that are genuinely fixed design decisions (feedback duration, velocity), static lets are fine. For constants that might become tunable (Kazez coefficients, initial offset range), constructor injection is more future-proof -- but also more complex for no immediate benefit.

I'd suggest starting with named static constants and promoting to injectable parameters only when a concrete need arises. The important thing right now is that these values have names and live in discoverable locations rather than being inline literals.

---

Want me to proceed with the glossary/architecture/project-context improvements, or would you rather discuss the extraction approach for these constants first?

### 🤖 Assistant (2026-03-05T22:29)

A few things I want to flag and get your input on:

**The pitch bend coupling is the most dangerous finding.** The value `2` in `sendPitchBendRange()` at `SoundFontNotePlayer.swift:182`, the `200.0` guard in `SoundFontPlaybackHandle.swift:55`, and the `200.0` divisor in `pitchBendValue()` at `SoundFontNotePlayer.swift:199` all encode "±2 semitones = ±200 cents" -- but they're not connected. If someone changed the RPN to 4 semitones, two other places would silently break. A single `pitchBendRangeSemitones` constant that derives the others would eliminate this. Do you agree this is worth addressing, or is the pitch bend range effectively frozen?

**The cold-start difficulty disconnect.** `PerceptualNote.currentDifficulty` defaults to `100.0` (line 158), which happens to equal `TrainingSettings.maxCentDifference`. But they're not connected -- changing the max to 80 wouldn't change the cold start. Is the intent that cold start always equals max difficulty? If so, the default should reference `TrainingSettings` rather than being a coincidental literal.

**The initialCentOffsetRange discrepancy.** The code says `±20.0` cents (`PitchMatchingSession.swift:54`), but the glossary says "Random within ±100 cents for v0.2." Which is current? If ±20 is intentional, the glossary needs updating. If it was narrowed from ±100 for usability reasons, that decision should be documented somewhere.

**On the grouping question.** I proposed four groupings (shared training, algorithm, pitch matching, audio). But I'm second-guessing whether `TrainingConstants` is the right home for `feedbackDuration` and `velocity`. These are really session playback parameters, not training logic. An alternative: put them directly on the `TrainingSession` protocol as default requirements, or leave them where they are but as named constants instead of literals. What feels right to you?

**On `1200.0` (cents per octave).** This appears in `PitchMatchingSession` (twice) and `TuningSystem` (twice). It's a musical physics constant, like pi. I'd lean toward `Cents.perOctave` as a static constant on the `Cents` type itself. Seems like a natural home. Thoughts?

**On the Kazez coefficients.** Do you want these to be documented with the academic source? I'm assuming the formula comes from Daniel Kazez's work on ear training, but I don't want to attribute it incorrectly. What's the actual provenance?

<a id="msg-assistant-163"></a>

### 🤖 Assistant (2026-03-05T22:51)

<details>
<summary>💭 Thinking</summary>

The test creates records at 72h, 48h, and 47h ago, expecting 2 day buckets. The `recentThreshold` is 24h. Records at 48h and 72h are both older than 24h and younger than 7 days, so they should be bucketed by day. The 48h and 47h records should be on the same calendar day, and the 72h record on a different day → 2 buckets.

But wait - this is time-sensitive. If the test runs at certain times of day, 48h ago and 47h ago might cross a calendar day boundary. For example, if it's 1:00 AM, then 48h ago is 1:00 AM two days ago, and 47h ago is 2:00 AM two days ago - same day. But if it's 0:30 AM, then 48h ago is 0:30 AM two days ago, and 47h ago is 1:30 AM two days ago - still same day.


Actually, I see the real problem now. Since 48h and 47h differ by just 1 hour, they'd only land on different calendar days if 48h ago falls right before midnight. If the test runs between 11 PM and midnight, then 48h ago would be 11 PM two days prior while 47h ago would be midnight the next day - splitting them across a day boundary and creating 3 buckets instead of 2.

The solution is to use time windows that can't accidentally span a midnight boundary, like 48h and 48.5h, or better yet, pick hours that are guaranteed to stay within the same calendar day. to be on the same calendar day regardless of when the test runs. We could use 49 and 48 (differ by 1h - but same issue). 

Better approach: use 48.5 and 48.0 - they differ by 30 min, so they'll always be on the same day. Actually no, the same problem exists if one is at 23:45 and the other at 00:15.

The safest fix: make the two "same day" records differ by less than the minimum possible time to midnight from any starting point. But that's not really possible with hour granularity.

Better approach: make the records at times like `hoursAgo: 48` and `hoursAgo: 48` with the same offset, or use the calendar to construct dates explicitly at noon on specific days.

Actually, the simplest fix is to just make the two records at `hoursAgo: 50` and `hoursAgo: 49` (or `hoursAgo: 60` and `hoursAgo: 59`), where both are well within the same calendar day regardless of current time. If the current time is T, then T-50h and T-49h differ by 1h. This still has the same problem near midnight.

The real fix is to use `startOfDay` offsets instead. Let me check how `makePitchComparisonRecord` actually works to see if I can construct the dates more explicitly.

</details>

<a id="msg-assistant-198"></a>

### 🤖 Assistant (2026-03-05T22:56)

<details>
<summary>💭 Thinking</summary>

Now I have a clear picture. Let me plan the changes carefully.

Key decisions:
1. **PerceptualNote internal fields**: The `mean`, `stdDev`, `m2` fields are used in Welford's algorithm with raw arithmetic. Wrapping them in `Cents` would add `.rawValue` noise everywhere. Better to keep them as `Double` internally and only use `Cents` at interface boundaries. Actually, wait - `mean` is accessed externally (e.g., `statsForNote(MIDINote($0)).mean`). Let me check...

The `mean` field is used:
- In `averageThreshold` to compute an average, then converted to `Int`


- In `weakSpots` to sort notes by score
- In `update()` for Welford's algorithm

Since `Cents` doesn't support arithmetic operators (+, -, *, /), wrapping these fields would be very noisy. I'll leave `PerceptualNote` internals as `Double` but change the protocol-level interfaces. The protocol methods like `update(note:centOffset:isCorrect:)` and `overallMean` should accept and return `Cents` conceptually, so I need to handle the conversion at those boundaries.

The real question is whether it's worth the friction—if `overallMean` returns `Cents?`, consumers need `.rawValue` to do math, and internally I'm constantly wrapping and unwrapping. But using `Cents` in the protocol signatures does communicate intent clearly, so I think the trade-off is worth it for data types and protocol interfaces even if the implementation stays as `Double` underneath.

For `referenceFrequency`, switching to `Frequency?` makes sense. And `NotePlayer`'s duration should become `NoteDuration` since it's a protocol boundary. But `feedbackDuration` is trickier—it's really just a UI timing constant, not semantically a note duration, so using Swift's built-in `Duration` would be cleaner, though that changes how I call `Task.sleep` with it.

Looking at what's actually worth doing, I should focus on the high-impact changes: renaming `NotePlayer.play(duration:)` to use `NoteDuration`, converting the cent-related `Double` values to `Cents` across `CompletedPitchMatching`, `PitchMatchingChallenge`, and the session types, and updating `referenceFrequency` to `Frequency?`. I'm also converting the session best error fields to use `Cents?` for consistency.

For the medium-impact protocol changes, I need to update the profile methods to accept `Cents` instead of `Double` for cent offsets and difficulties, and convert the computed properties like `overallMean` and `matchingStdDev` to return `Cents?` instead of raw doubles.

For the lower-impact items, I should leave `PerceptualNote`'s internal fields as `Double` since Welford's algorithm would become too noisy with the conversion. But I'm noticing `averageThreshold(noteRange:)` returns `Int?` which seems wrong—it should return `Cents?` since it's averaging cent values. Now I'm checking how `currentDifficulty` works: it's a computed property that gets the magnitude of a `Cents` offset, and since `Cents.magnitude` returns `Double`, there's a type mismatch I need to resolve.

Looking at the practical changes with the best return on investment, I should focus on updating the duration parameter in `NotePlayer.play()`, converting the cent-related fields in `CompletedPitchMatching` and `PitchMatchingChallenge`, adding proper `Frequency?` and `Cents?` types to the session properties, and standardizing the feedback duration fields across both classes.

The tricky part is that protocol changes will cascade through all conformances and call sites. Since `PitchComparisonProfile` and `PitchMatchingProfile` each have only one conformance in `PerceptualProfile`, that's manageable. For `NotePlayer`, I need to account for `SoundFontNotePlayer` and any test doubles. I'm also realizing that `Cents` doesn't support arithmetic operations, which might limit how I can use it in certain calculations.

Let me start with the implementation in dependency order: first the `Cents` type and data structures, then the protocols, then the implementations. I'll group changes by file to minimize back-and-forth.

For the highest-impact changes, I should tackle `NotePlayer` duration conversion first—changing from `TimeInterval` to `NoteDuration` and cascading that through `PitchComparisonSession` and `PitchMatchingSession`. Then I'll handle the `CompletedPitchMatching` type updates for cent offsets and errors.

</details>

**Group 1: NotePlayer duration → NoteDuration**


Files: NotePlayer.swift, MockNotePlayer.swift, PitchComparisonSession.swift (currentNoteDuration + playPitchComparisonNotes), PitchMatchingSession.swift (currentNoteDuration), NotePlayerConvenienceTests.swift, ExtensionOnlyNotePlayer in tests

Now I'm realizing that `NoteDuration` enforces a clamped range of 0.3-3.0 seconds, which means test values like 0.01, 0.5, 0.3, and 10.0 would all get clamped to fit within those bounds. This breaks tests that expect zero or negative durations to throw errors, since the clamping would prevent those edge cases from being tested properly.

The real issue is that `NoteDuration` is a user-settings type with built-in validation, but using it in the protocol would prevent the protocol from accepting invalid durations for testing or other purposes. The protocol should accept raw `TimeInterval` values and handle its own validation, keeping the clamping logic at the settings layer where it belongs. If I use `NoteDuration`, the guard statement checking for positive duration becomes redundant since `NoteDuration` is always >= 0.3 by design.

I'll keep `NotePlayer.play(duration:)` accepting `TimeInterval` as-is. The sessions already unwrap `NoteDuration` to its raw value at the call site, which is the right boundary for this conversion. Now I need to focus on the other refactoring groups, starting with converting data types to cents.

For the pitch matching types, I'm converting `initialCentOffset` and `userCentError` from `Double` to `Cents`. In `PitchMatchingSession`, I need to change `referenceFrequency` to `Frequency?` and `sessionBestCentError` to `Cents?`, then update all the places these are used. For `PitchComparisonSession`, I'm converting `sessionBestCentDifference` to `Cents?` while keeping `currentDifficulty` as `Double?` since it returns a magnitude value. Let me trace through how these properties are actually consumed to make sure the conversions make sense.

Now I'm looking at the remaining type conversions: `feedbackDuration` needs to become `Duration`, and across the profile protocols I'm updating multiple cent-related parameters like `centOffset`, `centError`, and the statistical properties like `overallMean` and `overallStdDev` to use the `Cents` type instead of `Double`.

I'm concerned about the scope of Group 5 since it touches so many protocol methods. Let me trace through how `overallMean` is actually used in the views and strategy code to understand the impact—specifically, I'm noticing that `KazezNoteStrategy` clamps `profileMean` against a `Double` range, so if the protocol returns `Cents?` instead, I'll need to unwrap the raw value before clamping.

Given this trade-off between type safety and verbosity, I think the pragmatic approach is to convert the data model types and observable state properties that views directly consume, change `feedbackDuration` to `Duration`, but be selective about protocol interfaces—only updating them where the clarity gain justifies the extra `.rawValue` unwrapping throughout the codebase. Let me check how the views actually access `sessionBestCentError` and `sessionBestCentDifference` to see if those should be included in this pass.

Let me reconsider whether these profile properties should actually be `Cents?`. Conceptually they should be—`overallMean` is the mean of cent offsets, `overallStdDev` is the standard deviation of those same offsets, `matchingMean` is the mean of absolute cent errors, and `matchingStdDev` is its standard deviation. They're all measuring the same units. The tricky part is that PerceptualProfile calculates these by summing and averaging Double values...

Computing the mean...

If I change the return type to `Cents?`, I'd need to wrap the final computed value in the `Cents` type. Then in KazezNoteStrategy, accessing that value would require one extra `.rawValue` unwrap to get back to the Double for clamping.

Now looking at how `PitchComparisonProfile.update(centOffset:)` gets called from PerceptualProfile—the offset is already a `Cents` type, but the caller extracts its magnitude as a Double and would need to wrap it back. It makes more sense to pass the `Cents` value directly and let the update method handle the sign and magnitude logic internally.

For `averageThreshold(noteRange:)`, converting it from `Int?` to `Cents?` would be cleaner, but since this method isn't actually used in production code—only in the protocol definition and tests—it might be dead code that I should reconsider keeping.

1. **PitchMatchingSessionTests.swift** - Tests that compare `result.userCentError` with numeric literals. Wait, actually... `Cents: ExpressibleByIntegerLiteral`, so `0` can be `Cents(0)`. And `Cents: Comparable`, so `Cents > Cents` works. 

But the real issue is that `Cents` doesn't support arithmetic operations—there's no `-` operator defined, so expressions like `abs(result.userCentError - challenge.initialCentOffset)` won't compile. I need to either add basic arithmetic operators to `Cents` or find another way to handle these calculations.

Option (a) feels right since it makes `Cents` a proper domain type with the operations it actually needs: subtraction for difference calculations, absolute value for magnitude, and comparison for sign testing. The tests require these operations specifically, so it's not over-engineering—it's just making the type functional. I'm realizing that `Cents` can use `ExpressibleByIntegerLiteral` to make comparisons like `userCentError > 0` work directly, but arithmetic operations like `abs()` and subtraction won't work since `Cents` doesn't implement `SignedNumeric` or the necessary operators. So the tests will need to access `.rawValue` for any calculations involving the cent values.

<a id="msg-assistant-397"></a>

### 🤖 Assistant (2026-03-05T23:10)

Here's a summary of both passes and what was accomplished:

## Pass 1 + Pass 2 Summary

### Pass 1: Constant extraction and naming
- **`Cents.perOctave`** — replaces magic `1200.0` throughout
- **`TrainingConstants`** — shared `feedbackDuration` and `velocity`
- **`SoundFontNotePlayer.pitchBendRangeSemitones/pitchBendRangeCents`** — single source of truth for MIDI pitch bend coupling
- **`PerceptualNote.coldStartDifficulty`** — named constant
- **`ProgressTimeline` bucket thresholds** — named constants
- **`KazezNoteStrategy` coefficients** — named with Kazez citation
- **`TrainingModeConfig` defaults** — extracted shared EWMA/session-gap values
- **`MIDINote.validRange`** usage instead of hardcoded `127`/`128`

### Pass 2: Raw-type refactoring
**Domain types threaded through interfaces:**
- `PitchMatchingSession.referenceFrequency`: `Double?` → `Frequency?`
- `PitchMatchingSession.sessionBestCentError`: `Double?` → `Cents?`
- `PitchComparisonSession.sessionBestCentDifference`: `Double?` → `Cents?`
- `PitchComparisonSession.currentDifficulty/lastCompletedCentDifference`: `Double?` → `Cents?`
- `CompletedPitchMatching.initialCentOffset/userCentError`: `Double` → `Cents`
- `PitchMatchingChallenge.initialCentOffset`: `Double` → `Cents`
- `PitchComparisonProfile` protocol: all cent parameters/returns → `Cents`
- `PitchMatchingProfile` protocol: all cent parameters/returns → `Cents`
- `PerceptualProfile` conformances updated accordingly
- `TrainingStatsView`: `Double?` → `Cents?`
- `PitchMatchingFeedbackIndicator`: `Double?` → `Cents?`
- `TrainingConstants.feedbackDuration`: `TimeInterval` → `Duration`
- Both sessions use `Duration` directly with `Task.sleep(for:)`

**Test fixes:**
- `dayBuckets` flaky test: fixed with calendar-day-aligned timestamps
- All test mock profiles updated for `Cents` signatures
- Test assertions use `.rawValue` for arithmetic on `Cents`

**Deliberate non-changes:**
- `NotePlayer.play(duration:)` stays `TimeInterval` — `NoteDuration` clamps to 0.3-3.0 which would break tests and limit the protocol unnecessarily
- `PerceptualNote` internal fields stay `Double` — Welford's algorithm arithmetic would be too noisy with `Cents` wrapper
- Persistence records (`PitchMatchingRecord`, `PitchComparisonRecord`) stay `Double` — these are SwiftData boundary types

**29 files changed, 960/960 tests pass.**

Shall I proceed with the remaining review items (glossary, architecture.md, project-context.md updates)?

Let me now plan my updates:

## 1. Glossary Updates
- Remove stale entries: Note1/Note2, Narrowing Factor, Widening Factor, Current Difficulty, Regional Range, Range Mean, Natural vs. Mechanical, Adaptive Note Strategy
- Add missing entries: Training Mode, TrainingModeConfig, ProgressTimeline, Kazez Note Strategy, EWMA, TimeBucket/BucketSize, DirectedInterval

- Update Weak Spot and Perceptual Profile definitions, and correct Initial Cent Offset from ±100 to ±20

## 2. Architecture Updates

I need to add ProgressTimeline, TrainingConstants, and TrainingModeConfig to the project structure section, update the domain types to reflect how Cents, Frequency, and Duration thread through the system, and consolidate the historical amendments since the document is quite large.

## 3. Project Context Updates
I'm adding ProgressTimeline to the view dependencies, documenting the PitchMatchingSession state machine, generalizing session statements, incorporating interval training context, clarifying that feedbackDuration applies to both modes, and updating how domain types are used throughout.

## 4. check-dependencies.sh
The feature directory is actually named PitchComparison, not Comparison, so I need to fix that check. I also need to add validation for print() calls, broaden the cross-feature dependency checks, and verify that code is importing OSLog instead of the os module.

Looking at the script, I'm catching several naming inconsistencies: line 89 checks for "Comparison" when it should be "PitchComparison", and the FEATURES array on line 113 has the same issue. The SCREEN_TYPES array also needs updating from "ComparisonScreen" to "PitchComparisonScreen".

For the logging imports, both `import os` and `import OSLog` are valid in Swift—`import os` gives access to the full os framework including Logger—so either approach works, but I should check what the code review actually recommended and align with that.

Now I'm ready to tackle all four document updates simultaneously.
